[2026-01-29T20:01:12Z] Akshay: Speaking about increased trade protectionism globally, and the return of economic statecraft and indeed economic warfare, the India Economy Survey alludes to the following: ↵ “The Y Decree was an economic sanction imposed by X on the city-state of Y around 432 ↵ BCE, just before the outbreak of the Z War. Under the decree, Y merchants were barred ↵ from markets and ports controlled by X, effectively cutting the city off from regional trade and severely damaging its economy. Although X justified the measure on religious and legal grounds (that Y were cultivating sacred land belonging to A and were harbouring runaway slaves), it was ↵ widely seen as a strategic attempt to assert dominance and punish Y, an ally of B. B demanded the repeal of the decree, and X’s refusal significantly escalated tensions, contributing to the onset of the war. The episode is often cited as one of the earliest examples of economic sanctions being used as a tool of statecraft, ↵ highlighting how trade restrictions can precipitate major geopolitical conflicts.”
